If you want to use LLVM on multiple\n36: /// threads simultaneously, you will need to use a separate PassRegistry on\n37: /// each thread.\n38: class PassRegistry {\n39:   mutable sys::SmartRWMutex<true> Lock;\n40: \n41:   /// PassInfoMap - Keep track of the PassInfo object for each registered pass.\n42:   using MapType = DenseMap<const void *, const PassInfo *>;\n43:   MapType PassInfoMap;\n44: \n45:   using StringMapType = StringMap<const PassInfo *>;\n46:   StringMapType PassInfoStringMap;\n47: \n48:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<const PassInfo>> ToFree;\n49:   std::vector<PassRegistrationListener *> Listeners;\n50: \n51: public:\n52:   PassRegistry() = default;\n53:   LLVM_ABI ~PassRegistry();\n54: \n55:   /// getPassRegistry - Access the global registry object, which is\n56:   /// automatically initialized at application launch and destroyed by\n57:   /// llvm_shutdown.\n58:   LLVM_ABI static PassRegistry *getPassRegistry();\n59: \n60:   /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n61:   /// type identifier (&MyPass::ID).\n62:   LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(const void *TI) const;\n63: \n64:   /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\n65:   /// argument string.\n66:   LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(StringRef Arg) const;\n67: \n68:   /// registerPass - Register a pass (by means of its PassInfo) with the\n69:   /// registry. External pass managers\n54: /// (PassManager and FunctionPassManager) are not represented here.\n55: /// Ordering of pass manager types is important here.\n56: enum PassManagerType {\n57:   PMT_Unknown = 0,\n58:   PMT_ModulePassManager = 1, ///< MPPassManager\n59:   PMT_CallGraphPassManager,  ///< CGPassManager\n60:   PMT_FunctionPassManager,   ///< FPPassManager\n61:   PMT_LoopPassManager,       ///< LPPassManager\n62:   PMT_RegionPassManager,     ///< RGPassManager\n63:   PMT_Last\n64: };\n65: \n66: // Different types of passes.\n67: enum PassKind {\n68:   PT_Region,\n69:   PT_Loop,\n70:   PT_Function,\n71:   PT_CallGraphSCC,\n72:   PT_Module,\n73:   PT_PassManager\n74: };\n75: \n76: /// This enumerates the LLVM full LTO or ThinLTO optimization phases.\n77: enum class ThinOrFullLTOPhase {\n78:   /// No LTO/ThinLTO behavior needed.\n79:   None,\n80:   /// ThinLTO prelink (summary) phase.\n81:   ThinLTOPreLink,\n82:   /// ThinLTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n83:   ThinLTOPostLink,\n84:   /// Full LTO prelink phase.\n85:   FullLTOPreLink,\n86:   /// Full LTO postlink (backend compile) phase.\n87:   FullLTOPostLink\n88: };\n89: \n90: #ifndef NDEBUG\n91: const char *to_string(ThinOrFullLTOPhase Phase);\n92: #endif\n93: \n94: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n95: /// Pass interface - Implemented by all 'passes'.  Subclass this if you are an\n96: /// interprocedural optimization or you do not fit into any of the more\n97: /// constrained passes described below.\n98: ///\n99: class LLVM_ABI Pass {\n100:   AnalysisResolver *Resolver = nullptr;  // Used to resolve analysis\n101:   const void *PassID;\n102:   PassKind Kind;\n103: \n104: public:\n105:   explicit Pass(PassKind K, char &pid) : PassID(&pid), Kind(K) {}\n106:   Pass(const Pass &) = delete;\n107:   Pass &operator=(const Pass &) = delete;\n108:   virtual ~Pass();\n109: \n110:   PassKind getPassKind() const { return Kind; }\n111: \n112:   /// getPassName - Return a nice clean name for a pass.  This usually\n113:   /// implemented in terms of the name that is registered by one of the\n114:   /// Registration templates, but can be overloaded directly.\n115:   virtual StringRef getPassName() const;\n116: \n117:   /// Return a nice clean name for a pass\n118:   /// corresponding to that used to enable the pass in opt.\n119:   StringRef getPassArgument() const;\n120: \n121:   /// getPassID - Return the PassID number that corresponds to this pass.\n122:   AnalysisID getPassID() const {\n123:     return PassID;\n124:   }\n125: \n126:   /// doInitialization - Virtual method overridden by subclasses to do\n127:   /// any necessary initialization before any pass is run.\n128:   virtual bool doInitialization(Module &)  { return false; }\n129: \n130:   /// doFinalization - Virtual method overriden by subclasses to do any\n131:   /// necessary clean up after all passes have run.\n132:   virtual bool doFinalization(Module &) { return false; }\n133: \n134:   /// print - Print out the internal state of the pass.  This is called by\n135:   /// Analyze to print out the contents of an analysis.  Otherwise it is not\n136:   /// necessary to implement this method.  Beware that the module pointer MAY be\n137:   /// null.  This automatically forwards to a virtual function that does not\n138:   /// provide the Module* in case the analysis doesn't need it it can just be\n139:   /// ignored.\n140:   virtual void print(raw_ostream &OS, const Module *M) const;\n141: \n142:   void dump() const; // dump - Print to stderr.\n143: \n144:   /// createPrinterPass - Get a Pass appropriate to print the IR this\n145:   /// pass operates on (Module, Function or MachineFunction).\n146:   virtual Pass *createPrinterPass(raw_ostream &OS,\n147:                                   const std::string &Banner) const = 0;\n148: \n149:   /// Each pass is responsible for assigning a pass manager to itself.\n150:   /// PMS is the stack of available pass manager.\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/Pass.h%3FL1-150"}}}

These functions are invoked whenever a pass is loaded\n111:   /// or removed from the current executable.\n112:   virtual void passRegistered(const PassInfo *) {}\n113: \n114:   /// enumeratePasses - Iterate over the registered passes, calling the\n115:   /// passEnumerate callback on each PassInfo object.\n116:   LLVM_ABI void enumeratePasses();\n117: \n118:   /// passEnumerate - Callback function invoked when someone calls\n119:   /// enumeratePasses on this PassRegistrationListener object.\n120:   virtual void passEnumerate(const PassInfo *) {}\n121: };\n122: \n123: } // end namespace llvm\n124: \n125: #endif // LLVM_PASSSUPPORT_H\n126: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d@4152de6435984e9fc55431f4d74a7470d8ac05c0/-/blob/llvm/include/llvm/PassSupport.h%3FL1-150"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019xkmyygB4NQXTMCWwX2PdD","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: //===- PassManager.h - Pass management infrastructure -----------*- C++ -*-===//\\n2: //\\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\\n6: //\\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n8: /// \\\\file\\n9: ///\\n10: /// This header defines various interfaces for pass management in LLVM. There\\n11: /// is no \\\"pass\\\" interface in LLVM per se. Instead, an instance of any class\\n12: /// which supports a method to 'run' it over a unit of IR can be used as\\n13: /// a pass. A pass manager is generally a tool to collect a sequence of passes\\n14: /// which run over a particular IR construct, and run each of them in sequence\\n15: /// over each such construct in the containing IR construct. As there is no\\n16: /// containing IR construct for a Module, a manager for passes over modules\\n17: /// forms the base case which runs its managed passes in sequence over the\\n18: /// single module provided.\\n19: ///\\n20: /// The core IR library provides managers for running passes over\\n21: /// modules and functions.\\n22: ///\\n23: /// * FunctionPassManager can run over a Module, runs each pass over\\n24: ///   a Function.\\n25: /// * ModulePassManager must be directly run, runs each pass over the Module.\\n26: ///\\n27: /// Note that the implementations of the pass managers use concept-based\\n28: /// polymorphism as outlined in the \\\"Value Semantics and Concept-based\\n29: /// Polymorphism\\\" talk (or its abbreviated sibling \\\"Inheritance Is The Base\\n30: /// Class of Evil\\\") by Sean Parent:\\n31: /// * https://sean-parent.stlab.cc/papers-and-presentations\\n32: /// * http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_BpMYeUFXv8\\n33: /// * https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/shows/goingnative-2013/inheritance-base-class-of-evil\\n34: ///\\n35: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n36: \\n37: #ifndef LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n38: #define LLVM_IR_PASSMANAGER_H\\n39: \\n40: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\\\"\\n41: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\\\"\\n42: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/StringExtras.h\\\"\\n43: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\\\"\\n44: #include \\\"llvm/ADT/TinyPtrVector.h\\\"\\n45: #include \\\"llvm/IR/Analysis.h\\\"\\n46: #include \\\"llvm/IR/PassManagerInternal.h\\\"\\n47: #include \\\"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\\\"\\n48: #include \\\"llvm/Support/TypeName.h\\\"\\n49: #include <cassert>\\n50: #include <cstring>\\n51: #include <list>\\n52: #include <memory>\\n53: #include <tuple>\\n54: #include <type_traits>\\n55: #include <utility>\\n56: #include <vector>\\n57: \\n58: namespace llvm {\\n59: \\n60: class Function;\\n61: class Module;\\n62: \\n63: // Forward declare the analysis manager template.\\n64: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager;\\n65: \\n66: /// A CRTP mix-in to automatically provide informational APIs needed for\\n67: /// passes.\\n68: ///\\n69: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are passes.\\n70: template <typename DerivedT> struct PassInfoMixin {\\n71:   /// Gets the name of the pass we are mixed into.\\n72:   static StringRef name() {\\n73:     static_assert(std::is_base_of<PassInfoMixin, DerivedT>::value,\\n74:                   \\\"Must pass the derived type as the template argument!\\\");\\n75:     StringRef Name = getTypeName<DerivedT>();\\n76:     Name.consume_front(\\\"llvm::\\\");\\n77:     return Name;\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n81:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n82:     StringRef ClassName = DerivedT::name();\\n83:     auto PassName = MapClassName2PassName(ClassName);\\n84:     OS << PassName;\\n85:   }\\n86: };\\n87: \\n88: /// A CRTP mix-in that provides informational APIs needed for analysis passes.\\n89: ///\\n90: /// This provides some boilerplate for types that are analysis passes. It\\n91: /// automatically mixes in \\\\c PassInfoMixin.\\n92: template <typename DerivedT>\\n93: struct AnalysisInfoMixin : PassInfoMixin<DerivedT> {\\n94:   /// Returns an opaque, unique ID for this analysis type.\\n95:   ///\\n96:   /// This ID is a pointer type that is guaranteed to be 8-byte aligned and thus\\n97:   /// suitable for use in sets, maps, and other data structures that use the low\\n98:   /// bits of pointers.\\n99:   ///\\n100:   /// Note that this requires the derived type provide a static \\\\c AnalysisKey\\n101:   /// member called \\\\c Key.\\n102:   ///\\n103:   /// FIXME: The only reason the mixin type itself can't declare the Key value\\n104:   /// is that some compilers cannot correctly unique a templated static variable\\n105:   /// so it has the same addresses in each instantiation. The only currently\\n106:   /// known platform with this limitation is Windows DLL builds, specifically\\n107:   /// building each part of LLVM as a DLL. It is itself a valid pass over that unit of\\n151: /// IR, and when run over some given IR will run each of its contained passes in\\n152: /// sequence. Pass managers are the primary and most basic building block of a\\n153: /// pass pipeline.\\n154: ///\\n155: /// When you run a pass manager, you provide an \\\\c AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>\\n156: /// argument. The pass manager will propagate that analysis manager to each\\n157: /// pass it runs, and will call the analysis manager's invalidation routine with\\n158: /// the PreservedAnalyses of each pass it runs.\\n159: template <typename IRUnitT,\\n160:           typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>,\\n161:           typename... ExtraArgTs>\\n162: class PassManager : public PassInfoMixin<\\n163:                         PassManager<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>> {\\n164: public:\\n165:   /// Construct a pass manager.\\n166:   explicit PassManager() = default;\\n167: \\n168:   // FIXME: These are equivalent to the default move constructor/move\\n169:   // assignment. However, using = default triggers linker errors due to the\\n170:   // explicit instantiations below. Find away to use the default and remove the\\n171:   // duplicated code here.\\n172:   PassManager(PassManager &&Arg) : Passes(std::move(Arg.Passes)) {}\\n173: \\n174:   PassManager &operator=(PassManager &&RHS) {\\n175:     Passes = std::move(RHS.Passes);\\n176:     return *this;\\n177:   }\\n178: \\n179:   void printPipeline(raw_ostream &OS,\\n180:                      function_ref<StringRef(StringRef)> MapClassName2PassName) {\\n181:     ListSeparator LS(\\\",\\\");\\n182:     for (auto &P : Passes) {\\n183:       OS << LS;\\n184:       P->printPipeline(OS, MapClassName2PassName);\\n185:     }\\n186:   }\\n187: \\n188:   /// Run all of the passes in this manager over the given unit of IR.\\n189:   /// ExtraArgs are passed to each pass.\\n190:   PreservedAnalyses run(IRUnitT &IR, AnalysisManagerT &AM,\\n191:                         ExtraArgTs... ExtraArgs);\\n192: \\n193:   template <typename PassT>\\n194:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<!std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n195:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n196:     using PassModelT =\\n197:         detail::PassModel<IRUnitT, PassT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n198:     // Do not use make_unique or emplace_back, they cause too many template\\n199:     // instantiations, causing terrible compile times.\\n200:     Passes.push_back(std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>(\\n201:         new PassModelT(std::forward<PassT>(Pass))));\\n202:   }\\n203: \\n204:   /// When adding a pass manager pass that has the same type as this pass\\n205:   /// manager, simply move the passes over. This is because we don't have\\n206:   /// use cases rely on executing nested pass managers. Doing this could\\n207:   /// reduce implementation complexity and avoid potential invalidation\\n208:   /// issues that may happen with nested pass managers of the same type.\\n209:   template <typename PassT>\\n210:   LLVM_ATTRIBUTE_MINSIZE std::enable_if_t<std::is_same_v<PassT, PassManager>>\\n211:   addPass(PassT &&Pass) {\\n212:     for (auto &P : Pass.Passes)\\n213:       Passes.push_back(std::move(P));\\n214:   }\\n215: \\n216:   /// Returns if the pass manager contains any passes.\\n217:   bool isEmpty() const { return Passes.empty(); }\\n218: \\n219:   static bool isRequired() { return true; }\\n220: \\n221: protected:\\n222:   using PassConceptT =\\n223:       detail::PassConcept<IRUnitT, AnalysisManagerT, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n224: \\n225:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<PassConceptT>> Passes;\\n226: };\\n227: \\n228: template <typename IRUnitT>\\n229: void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace(raw_ostream &OS, const IRUnitT &IR);\\n230: \\n231: template <>\\n232: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Module>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n233:                                                    const Module &IR);\\n234: \\n235: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Module>;\\n236: \\n237: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over modules.\\n238: using ModulePassManager = PassManager<Module>;\\n239: \\n240: template <>\\n241: LLVM_ABI void printIRUnitNameForStackTrace<Function>(raw_ostream &OS,\\n242:                                                      const Function &IR);\\n243: \\n244: extern template class LLVM_TEMPLATE_ABI PassManager<Function>;\\n245: \\n246: /// Convenience typedef for a pass manager over functions.\\n247: using FunctionPassManager = PassManager<Function>;\\n248: \\n249: /// A container for analyses that lazily runs them and caches their\\n250: /// results.\\n251: ///\\n252: /// This class can manage analyses for any IR unit where the address of the IR\\n253: /// unit sufficies as its identity.\\n254: template <typename IRUnitT, typename... ExtraArgTs> class AnalysisManager {\\n255: public:\\n256:   class Invalidator;\\n257: \\n258: private:\\n259:   // Now that we've defined our invalidator, we can define the concept types.\\n260:   using ResultConceptT = detail::AnalysisResultConcept<IRUnitT, Invalidator>;\\n261:   using PassConceptT =\\n262:       detail::AnalysisPassConcept<IRUnitT, Invalidator, ExtraArgTs...>;\\n263: \\n264:   /// List of analysis pass IDs and associated concept pointers.\\n265:   ///\\n266:   /// Requires iterators to be valid across appending new entries and arbitrary\\n267:   /// erases. LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain\\n\\n### Overview\\nLLVM's optimization pass system uses a sophisticated chain of components to register, manage, and execute transformation passes. This trace covers both the legacy pass manager and the new pass manager (NPM) infrastructure.\\n\\n### 1. Pass Manager Template (llvm/include/llvm/IR/PassManager.h)\\nThe core PassManager is a template class that manages a sequence of passes over a particular unit of IR (Module, Function, Loop, etc.). Key aspects:\\n- **Template Definition** (lines 159-226): `template <typename IRUnitT, typename AnalysisManagerT = AnalysisManager<IRUnitT>, typename... ExtraArgTs> class PassManager`\\n- **addPass() Method** (lines 193-214): Adds passes to the manager using concept-based polymorphism, storing them in a vector of unique_ptr<PassConceptT>\\n- **run() Method** (lines 188-191): Declared here, implemented in PassManagerImpl.h\\n- **Type Aliases**: ModulePassManager (line 238), FunctionPassManager (line 247)\\n\\n### 2. PassRegistry (llvm/include/llvm/PassRegistry.h)\\nManages the registration and initialization of the pass subsystem. Key components:\\n- **getPassRegistry()** (line 58): Returns the global registry object initialized at application startup\\n- **registerPass()** (line 70): Registers a pass (by PassInfo) with the registry, required for use with PassManager\\n- **getPassInfo()** (lines 62, 66): Looks up a pass's PassInfo by type identifier or argument string\\n- **PassInfoMap** (line 43): DenseMap storing PassInfo objects indexed by pass type pointer\\n- **PassInfoStringMap** (line 45): StringMap for lookup by command-line argument\\n\\n### 3.
